     <p>
      <b>
       Faryl Smith
      </b>
      (born 23 July 1995) is a British
      <a href="/wiki/Mezzo-soprano" title="Mezzo-soprano">
       mezzo-soprano
      </a>
      who rose to fame after appearing on the second series of the
      <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">
       ITV
      </a>
      television talent show
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Got_Talent" title="Britain's Got Talent">
        Britain's Got Talent
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2008. She received praise throughout the competition, and although the favourite to win after the second round, she finished outside the top three in the live final on 31 May. During the competition, she was tutored by singing coach
      <a href="/wiki/Yvie_Burnett" title="Yvie Burnett">
       Yvie Burnett
      </a>
      and received offers from various record labels. After the show, she, unlike other finalists, did not sign with
      <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">
       Simon Cowell
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Syco" title="Syco">
       Syco
      </a>
      , although she did appear on fellow finalist
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnston_(singer)" title="Andrew Johnston (singer)">
       Andrew Johnston
      </a>
      's debut album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/One_Voice_(Andrew_Johnston_album)" title="One Voice (Andrew Johnston album)">
        One Voice
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Smith signed a contract with
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_Classics_and_Jazz" title="Universal Classics and Jazz">
       Universal Classics and Jazz
      </a>
      for a 2.3 million advance in December 2008, the largest ever granted to a schoolgirl. Her debut album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Faryl" title="Faryl">
        Faryl
       </a>
      </i>
      , was recorded from December 2008 to January 2009 and released in March 2009.
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      became the fastest-selling solo classical album in British chart history, selling 29,200 copies in the first week. It debuted at number six, but rose to number four in the following week, making Smith the third
      <i>
       Britain's Got Talent
      </i>
      contestant to have a top ten album. In 2010, on account of
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      , Smith was nominated for two Classical BRIT Awards and became the youngest artist ever to receive a double nomination.
     </p>
     <p>
      Smith's second album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Wonderland_(Faryl_Smith_album)" title="Wonderland (Faryl Smith album)">
        Wonderland
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released in November 2009. A concept album based on
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland" title="Alice in Wonderland">
        Alice in Wonderland
       </a>
      </i>
      , the album was well received by critics, but was not successful in the charts. After the release of
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      , Smith's contract with Universal ended. In addition to releasing her albums, she featured on a charity cover of "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Prayer_(Celine_Dion_and_Andrea_Bocelli_song)" title="The Prayer (Celine Dion and Andrea Bocelli song)">
       The Prayer
      </a>
      ", released in March 2010, provided vocals for the 2012 album
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Magic_of_a_Thousand_Strings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Magic of a Thousand Strings (page does not exist)">
        The Magic of a Thousand Strings
       </a>
      </i>
      by the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Harp_Ensemble&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Harp Ensemble (page does not exist)">
       International Harp Ensemble
      </a>
      , and has performed at numerous events, including the 2009
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Variety_Performance" title="Royal Variety Performance">
       Royal Variety Performance
      </a>
      . Smith lives with her parents in
      <a href="/wiki/Kettering" title="Kettering">
       Kettering
      </a>
      , where she is currently taking a
      <a href="/wiki/Gap_year" title="Gap year">
       gap year
      </a>
      and applying to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_conservatoires" title="Music conservatoires">
       music conservatoires
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Britain.27s_Got_Talent">
       <i>
        Britain's Got Talent
       </i>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Britain's Got Talent">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Before her appearance on television, Smith had performed competitively in the Kettering, Northamptonshire
      <a href="/wiki/Eisteddfod" title="Eisteddfod">
       Eisteddfod
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Llangollen_International_Musical_Eisteddfod" title="Llangollen International Musical Eisteddfod">
       Llangollen International Musical Eisteddfod
      </a>
      , the Pontins Junior Starquest competition and Festival 4 Stars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seven_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-seven-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She auditioned for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Got_Talent_(Series_2)" title="Britain's Got Talent (Series 2)">
       the second series
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">
       ITV
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reality_show" title="Reality show">
       reality show
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Got_Talent" title="Britain's Got Talent">
        Britain's Got Talent
       </a>
      </i>
      , giving what Jon O'Brien, of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">
       Allmusic
      </a>
      , called a "mature" performance of "
      <a href="/wiki/Ave_Maria_(Bach/Gounod)" title="Ave Maria (Bach/Gounod)">
       Ave Maria
      </a>
      ",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was put through to the live shows.
      <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">
       Simon Cowell
      </a>
      described her audition as "the best audition I've heard in years".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-too_much_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-too_much-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Before performing live, she and
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnston_(singer)" title="Andrew Johnston (singer)">
       Andrew Johnston
      </a>
      were favourites to win.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budding_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-budding-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She won her semi-final by the public vote, performing a cover of
      <a href="/wiki/Sarah_McLachlan" title="Sarah McLachlan">
       Sarah McLachlan
      </a>
      's "
      <a href="/wiki/Angel_(Sarah_McLachlan_song)" title="Angel (Sarah McLachlan song)">
       Angel
      </a>
      ". This placed her in the final,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times4033014_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-times4033014-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and left her as the favourite to win.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During her first live show, Cowell described her as "literally one in a million".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times4033014_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-times4033014-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She then performed in the live final, where she was described by Cowell as one of the five acts (along with
      <a href="/wiki/George_Sampson" title="George Sampson">
       George Sampson
      </a>
      , Johnston,
      <a href="/wiki/Signature_(dance_group)" title="Signature (dance group)">
       Signature
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kate_and_Gin" title="Kate and Gin">
       Kate and Gin
      </a>
      ) who had a chance of winning.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rocky_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rocky-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She again performed "Ave Maria",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seven_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-seven-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but finished outside the top three. Sampson eventually won the show as a result of the phone-in, with Signature second, and Johnston third.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rocky_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rocky-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a result of her final performance of "Ave Maria", Smith was invited to be a guest singer at a songwriting awards ceremony in London.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seven_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-seven-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She then went on to perform in the Britain's Got Talent Live Tour with other contestants,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      where she first performed a duet of "Walking in the Air" with Johnston.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="506" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg/220px-Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg/330px-Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg/440px-Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faryl_Smith_and_Andrew_Johnston_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Smith (right) and Johnston (left) on the Britain's Got Talent Live Tour, with host
        <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Mulhern" title="Stephen Mulhern">
         Stephen Mulhern
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      While Smith was competing in Britain's Got Talent, Cowell arranged for her to receive free singing lessons from leading vocal coach
      <a href="/wiki/Yvie_Burnett" title="Yvie Burnett">
       Yvie Burnett
      </a>
      , who had previously coached 2007
      <i>
       Britains Got Talent
      </i>
      winner
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Potts" title="Paul Potts">
       Paul Potts
      </a>
      and 2006
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">
        The X Factor
       </a>
      </i>
      winner
      <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">
       Leona Lewis
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secret_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-secret-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The story was broken by
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Mirror" title="The Sunday Mirror">
        The Sunday Mirror
       </a>
      </i>
      ; writing for the paper, Lara Gould characterised the lessons as "secret",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secret_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-secret-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while writers for
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Daily_Mail" title="The Daily Mail">
        The Daily Mail
       </a>
      </i>
      claimed that the lessons were "likely to upset fellow contestants", and were evidence that Smith was "already being groomed for stardom".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During her participation in the competition, Smith was offered record deals, but she and her family turned them down. Her father, Tony Smith, said "We have had offers from people interested in Faryl. But when Simon Cowell, the big man, says your daughter is special, you listen."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secret_10-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-secret-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cowell described Smith's potential career during the show, saying "I know she says
      <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Jenkins" title="Katherine Jenkins">
       Katherine [Jenkins]
      </a>
      is her idol but she is far better than her. She is by far the most talented youngster I've ever heard. When she opens her mouth her voice is just incredible."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-telegraph-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Record_deal">
       Record deal
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Record deal">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The day after the
      <i>
       Britain's Got Talent
      </i>
      finals,
      <a href="/wiki/Max_Clifford" title="Max Clifford">
       Max Clifford
      </a>
      , speaking for Simon Cowell, said that it was "quite possible" that Cowell would be signing some of the finalists, including Smith.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Though she did not sign with
      <a href="/wiki/Syco" title="Syco">
       Syco
      </a>
      , Cowell's record label, she did record a duet of "Walking in the Air" with Johnston, which appeared on his debut album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/One_Voice_(Andrew_Johnston_album)" title="One Voice (Andrew Johnston album)">
        One Voice
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnston_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Johnston-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was tipped as a potential
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christmas_number-one_singles_in_the_UK" title="Christmas number-one singles in the UK">
       Christmas number-one
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnston_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Johnston-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Before the release of
      <i>
       One Voice
      </i>
      , it was revealed that Smith and her father, Tony Smith, were finalising the details of her record deal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In November, it was announced that Smith would be performing on stage in Kettering with Sylvia Berryman, a vocal tutor who had worked with Smith prior to her appearance on
      <i>
       Britain's Got Talent
      </i>
      . Smith said that she was "really looking forward to singing locally again", and it was again reported that Smith hoped to soon sign her own record deal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-festive_duet_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-festive_duet-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In December 2008 the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">
        Daily Mail
       </a>
      </i>
      reported that Smith had signed a 2.3 million, multi-album deal with
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">
       Universal Music Group
      </a>
      that was the "most lucrative recording contract ever handed to a schoolgirl".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_signed_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DM_signed-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith said "I'm honoured to be joining such a fantastic record company, especially since it's where [Jenkins] started."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_signed_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DM_signed-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Dickon Stainer, speaking on behalf of Universal, said "as soon as we saw Faryl, it became an ambition to sign her."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_signed_18-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-DM_signed-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Universal claimed it intended to market Smith as a pop star.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-telegraph-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith signed the contract at the
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">
       Royal Albert Hall
      </a>
      , following which she performed with
      <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Jenkins" title="Katherine Jenkins">
       Katherine Jenkins
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_signed_18-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-DM_signed-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Neil Fisher, writing for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">
        The Times
       </a>
      </i>
      , described Smith as "heir apparent" to Jenkins;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the pair had first met when Smith won a competition at the Llangollen International Musical Eisteddfod. By 2009, Jenkins was acting as a mentor to Smith.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Foster-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In January 2009 plans were released for Smith to perform with
      <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Plcido Domingo">
       Plcido Domingo
      </a>
      , an idea originally suggested by him.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In an interview with the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Metro_(British_newspaper)" title="Metro (British newspaper)">
        Metro
       </a>
      </i>
      , Smith talked about her future plans, insisting that she did not wish to be dubbed as the next
      <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Church" title="Charlotte Church">
       Charlotte Church
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metro_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Metro-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She later said that "In the papers, it sounded like I was snobby when I said 'I don't want to be like Charlotte Church', but I didn't mean it like that."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lyons-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She has also spoken of her desire to appear in films on top of her musical career. She said "Films and movies are something I'd really like to do. I've always wanted to act so doing a film would be amazing."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metro_22-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Metro-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Faryl">
       <i>
        Faryl
       </i>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Faryl">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Faryl" title="Faryl">
       Faryl
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Smith's first album,
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      , was recorded at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Studios" title="Air Studios">
       Air Studios
      </a>
      , London,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_interview_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Independent_interview-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in December 2008, during Smith's Christmas holiday; it was completed on 3 January 2009 and features a 60-piece orchestra.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Red_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Red-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith described the song "River of Light" by saying that
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Danube" title="The Blue Danube">
        The Blue Danube
       </a>
      </i>
      "music now has words put to it. I like it because it's different. Everyone knows the tune and everybody has got high hopes for it."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lyons-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith said that her favourite song on the album was her version of the Welsh hymn, "
      <a href="/wiki/Calon_L%C3%A2n" title="Calon Ln">
       Calon Ln
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other songs include Smith's version of "
      <a href="/wiki/Amazing_Grace" title="Amazing Grace">
       Amazing Grace
      </a>
      ", a cover of
      <a href="/wiki/John_Denver" title="John Denver">
       John Denver
      </a>
      's "
      <a href="/wiki/Annie%27s_Song" title="Annie's Song">
       Annie's Song
      </a>
      ", and a version of "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Way_Old_Friends_Do" title="The Way Old Friends Do">
       The Way Old Friends Do
      </a>
      ", rewritten for Smith by
      <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Ulvaeus" title="Bjrn Ulvaeus">
       Bjrn Ulvaeus
      </a>
      . Smith spoke about the song, saying "It was about divorce ... They didn't think it was appropriate for me to sing about that, so Bjrn changed the lyrics so it's about friendship."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster_20-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Foster-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album was produced by Jon Cohen, who had previously worked with artists including the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operababes" title="Operababes">
       Operababes
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanessa_Mae" title="Vanessa Mae">
       Vanessa Mae
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_3-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Promotion began in January, with performances at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandarin_Oriental_Hotel#The_Mandarin_Oriental.2C_Hyde_Park" title="Mandarin Oriental Hotel">
       Mandarin Oriental Hotel
      </a>
      and appearances at the debut of
      <a href="/wiki/Oliver!#2009_London_revival" title="Oliver!">
       2009 London revival of
       <i>
        Oliver!
       </i>
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Red_26-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Red-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A television advert and music video for "River of Light" were recorded to further publicise the release, and Smith appeared on the cover of April's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Classic_FM_Magazine" title="Classic FM Magazine">
        Classic FM Magazine
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      More promotional appearances in the weeks leading up to the release of
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      included
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Loose_Women" title="Loose Women">
        Loose Women
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Paul_O%27Grady_Show" title="The Paul O'Grady Show">
        The Paul O'Grady Show
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">
       BBC Radio 4
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Five_Live" title="Radio Five Live">
       Radio Five Live
      </a>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Breakfast" title="BBC Breakfast">
        BBC Breakfast
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loose_Women_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Loose_Women-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She also appeared at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Children%27s_Champion_Awards" title="Children's Champion Awards">
       Children's Champion Awards
      </a>
      and met
      <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">
       Gordon Brown
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/10_Downing_Street" title="10 Downing Street">
       10 Downing Street
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Morgan-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Living_the_Dream_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Living_the_Dream-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On the day of the release, there was an album signing in Smith's hometown of
      <a href="/wiki/Kettering" title="Kettering">
       Kettering
      </a>
      , at the
      <a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">
       HMV
      </a>
      branch.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster_20-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Foster-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith said "I definitely want to be at home for the launch. I want to be surrounded by my friends and family because obviously, it's a big deal for me."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Living_the_Dream_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Living_the_Dream-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Pete Paphides, writing for
      <i>
       The Times
      </i>
      , said that the songs were performed "with power and restraint" and that the "arrangements by Jon Cohen suggest some kind of aesthetic endeavour beyond the basic thing for which they exist". He compared it favourably to three other
      <a href="/wiki/Mothering_Sunday" title="Mothering Sunday">
       Mothering Sunday
      </a>
      releases:
      <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Richie" title="Lionel Richie">
       Lionel Richie
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Just_Go_(Lionel_Richie_album)" title="Just Go (Lionel Richie album)">
        Just Go
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ronan_Keating" title="Ronan Keating">
       Ronan Keating
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Songs_for_My_Mother" title="Songs for My Mother">
        Songs for My Mother
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Barry_Manilow" title="Barry Manilow">
       Barry Manilow
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Greatest_Songs_of_the_Eighties" title="The Greatest Songs of the Eighties">
        The Greatest Songs of the Eighties
       </a>
      </i>
      . He awarded
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      3 out of a possible 5, the highest rating of the four.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Retailers in the United Kingdom ordered more than 80,000 copies of the album in the week before release, which Simon Cable, writing for the
      <i>
       Daily Mail
      </i>
      , noted was more copies than
      <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">
       U2
      </a>
      's recent
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/No_Line_on_the_Horizon" title="No Line on the Horizon">
        No Line on the Horizon
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cable_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cable-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also topped the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon.co.uk" title="Amazon.co.uk">
       Amazon.co.uk
      </a>
      presale chart.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cable_33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cable-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On the day of the release the album was at the number one spot on the
      <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">
       UK Albums Chart
      </a>
      , based on presales alone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan_30-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Morgan-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album became the fastest-selling classical solo album in British history, selling 20,000 copies in the first four days. The previous record holder had been
      <a href="/wiki/Hayley_Westenra" title="Hayley Westenra">
       Hayley Westenra
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pure_(Hayley_Westenra_album)" title="Pure (Hayley Westenra album)">
        Pure
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first week resulted in sales of 29,200 copies, which is higher than any other debut album of a classical singer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      officially entered the charts at number six and rose to fourth place the next week.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukcharts_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ukcharts-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Holden-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The success of the album left Smith the third
      <i>
       Britain's Got Talent
      </i>
      contestant to achieve a top ten album, after Potts (with
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/One_Chance_(album)" title="One Chance (album)">
        One Chance
       </a>
      </i>
      ) and Johnston (with
      <i>
       One Voice
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_3-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 2009 Smith travelled to Los Angeles to begin her promotion of
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      in the United States. She appeared on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">
        The Ellen DeGeneres Show
       </a>
      </i>
      in early May as part of her promotional tour.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      was released in the US on 5 May. Smith said before the release that she did not expect it to sell as well as it did in the UK. She said that "in the US it's a lot harder because I'm not as well-known."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith travelled back to the UK in early May,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-up_for_the_cup_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-up_for_the_cup-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and, on 23 May,
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      peaked at 31st place on
      <a href="/wiki/Top_Heatseekers" title="Top Heatseekers">
       Top Heatseekers
      </a>
      Albums chart and at sixth place on the Classical Albums chart, remaining in the charts for one and 17 weeks respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith opened the 2009
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_BRIT_Awards" title="Classical BRIT Awards">
       Classical BRIT Awards
      </a>
      , where, according to Elisa Roche of the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Daily_Express" title="Daily Express">
        Daily Express
       </a>
      </i>
      , she "captivated the best names in classical music".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She is the youngest performer ever to sing at the Classical BRITs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 30 May, Smith became the youngest person to sing the United Kingdom
      <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">
       national anthem
      </a>
      , "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/God_Save_The_Queen" title="God Save The Queen">
       God Save The Queen
      </a>
      ", at an
      <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">
       FA Cup
      </a>
      final when she performed during the opening ceremony at the
      <a href="/wiki/2009_FA_Cup_Final" title="2009 FA Cup Final">
       2009 final
      </a>
      , held in the
      <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">
       Wembley Stadium
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In June, Smith performed a duet with
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carreras" title="Jos Carreras">
       Jos Carreras
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Court_Palace_Festival" title="Hampton Court Palace Festival">
       Hampton Court Palace Festival
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cripps_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cripps-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in July, she attended the O2 Silver Clef Awards, winning the Classical Award.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In February 2010, after the release of Smith's second album,
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      was nominated for a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_BRIT_Awards" title="Classical BRIT Awards">
       Classical BRIT Award
      </a>
      in the album category. The category is voted for by the public, and the shortlist comprises the ten best-selling classical albums of the previous year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      lost to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Only_Men_Aloud" title="Only Men Aloud">
       Only Men Aloud
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Band_of_Brothers_(Only_Men_Aloud!_album)" title="Band of Brothers (Only Men Aloud! album)">
        Band of Brothers
       </a>
      </i>
      . Smith also lost in the young British classical performer category to
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Liebeck" title="Jack Liebeck">
       Jack Liebeck
      </a>
      , a violinist.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith became the youngest artist ever to receive a double nomination.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In November, Smith was awarded the best classical award at the 2009
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Variety_Club" title="Variety Club">
       Variety Club
      </a>
      awards,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the youngest ever recipient in the awards' 57-year history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cripps_45-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cripps-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Wonderland">
       <i>
        Wonderland
       </i>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Wonderland">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Wonderland_(Faryl_Smith_album)" title="Wonderland (Faryl Smith album)">
       Wonderland (Faryl Smith album)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In July 2009 it was announced that Smith was hoping to release her second album later in the year. In an interview, she expressed surprise and pleasure that the label wanted her to do another album so soon after the first.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In September, further details about the album were released, including its name,
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      , and planned release date, 30 November. Smith claimed that
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      "was an introduction to me and an introduction for me to recording", while Cohen, producer of both
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      , said Smith had "matured as an artist since the first album and I have no doubt that once again, people will be astonished and moved by her performances".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album, which was recorded at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarm_Studios" title="Sarm Studios">
       Sarm Studios
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Notting_Hill" title="Notting Hill">
       Notting Hill
      </a>
      , London, was completed in early October,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Take_That_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Take_That-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is loosely based on
      <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Carroll" title="Lewis Carroll">
       Lewis Carroll
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland" title="Alice in Wonderland">
        Alice in Wonderland
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jackson-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      was released on 30 November.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodjohn_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Goodjohn-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To publicise the album, Smith appeared on numerous radio shows, as well as television appearances including
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ready_Steady_Cook" title="Ready Steady Cook">
        Ready Steady Cook
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Peter" title="Blue Peter">
        Blue Peter
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_News_Channel" title="BBC News Channel">
       BBC News Channel
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Alan_Titchmarsh_Show" title="The Alan Titchmarsh Show">
        The Alan Titchmarsh Show
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sky_News_Sunrise" title="Sky News Sunrise">
        Sky News Sunrise
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodjohn_56-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Goodjohn-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      was well received by critics; Paul Callan, reviewing the album for the
      <i>
       Daily Express
      </i>
      , described it as "a joy". He compared it to other Christmas albums, saying that "[t]oo many are tired, much-repeated carol selections." He described Smith's "control, tone and warmth" as "very moving".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Andy Gill, reviewing
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">
        The Independent
       </a>
      </i>
      , gave a less positive review. He said that the influence of
      <i>
       Alice in Wonderland
      </i>
      was often hard to perceive and that Cohen and Smith had "sweetened the classical elements". However, he praised the arrangements of "Adiemus", "Barcarolle", "Merry Christmas, Mr Lawrence" and "Blow The Wind Southerly", but noted that on tracks including "Close To You", "the lack of emotional weight is telling." Overall, Gill gave
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      3 out of 5.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the album failed to perform as well as
      <i>
       Faryl
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edge-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      appearing on the top 75 of the UK Albums Chart for only one week, and peaked at 54th place.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-occ_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-occ-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After
      <i>
       Wonderland
      </i>
      , Smith's contract with Universal ended, and she subsequently received less attention from the press. Smith described the break with the label as mainly her decision, as she needed to focus on her A levels, which would allow her to got to university, explaining in an interview that "It wasn't like it ended horribly."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_59-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edge-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Smith performed at the 2009
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Variety_Performance" title="Royal Variety Performance">
       Royal Variety Performance
      </a>
      in front of
      <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
       Queen Elizabeth II
      </a>
      , where she sang "God Save the Queen" with
      <a href="/wiki/The_Soldiers" title="The Soldiers">
       The Soldiers
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She later said that the experience, including subsequently meeting the Queen, as the highlight of her year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thanks_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-thanks-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith also performed elsewhere with The Soldiers, including at
      <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul's Cathedral">
       St Paul's Cathedral
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Great Ormond Street Children's Hospital">
       Great Ormond Street Children's Hospital
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thanks_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-thanks-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22The_Prayer.22_and_The_Magic_of_a_Thousand_Strings">
       "The Prayer" and
       <i>
        The Magic of a Thousand Strings
       </i>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title='Edit section: "The Prayer" and The Magic of a Thousand Strings'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In the aftermath of the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">
       2010 Haiti earthquake
      </a>
      , Smith and 22 other classical musicians from the UK recorded a cover version of "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Prayer_(Celine_Dion_and_Andrea_Bocelli_song)" title="The Prayer (Celine Dion and Andrea Bocelli song)">
       The Prayer
      </a>
      ", which was released for download on 14 March. The proceeds of the single went to the
      <a href="/wiki/Disasters_Emergency_Committee" title="Disasters Emergency Committee">
       Disasters Emergency Committee
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith said "It's a real honour to be a part of something that is being done for the first time, and I hope that all music lovers get involved and help raise money for the campaign. I really hope that we can make a difference together to help the horrible situation that Haiti is in at the moment."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The group, dubbed "Classical
      <a href="/wiki/Band_Aid_(band)" title="Band Aid (band)">
       Band Aid
      </a>
      ",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joins_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-joins-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      recorded the track at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolis_Studios" title="Metropolis Studios">
       Metropolis Studios
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unite_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-unite-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and were backed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Royal Philharmonic Orchestra">
       Royal Philharmonic Orchestra
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joins_65-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-joins-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each vocalist in the group performed their own solo lines, and the entire group came together for the finale.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unite_66-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-unite-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "The Prayer" was the first ever classical charity single; Smith noted that "Pop singers do things like this a lot but it's unusual for classical singers to get involved so I've been really excited."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the summer of 2010 Smith performed at various festivals and events. Her father stated that "because she is still so young, we don't want her doing complete shows on her own and we don't want her doing too much."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-series_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-series-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Appearances included the Mercedes-Benz World Summer Concert in
      <a href="/wiki/Weybridge" title="Weybridge">
       Weybridge
      </a>
      on 4 July, That Glorious Noise charity concert in aid of
      <a href="/wiki/Muscular_dystrophy" title="Muscular dystrophy">
       muscular dystrophy
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes" title="Cleethorpes">
       Cleethorpes
      </a>
      on 17 July and the Last Night of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hampstead_Heath#Kenwood" title="Hampstead Heath">
       Kenwood
      </a>
      Proms on 21 August,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-series_68-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-series-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as well as the wedding of
      <a href="/wiki/Eamonn_Holmes" title="Eamonn Holmes">
       Eamonn Holmes
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Langsford" title="Ruth Langsford">
       Ruth Langsford
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith also opened the Serenata festival.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Angela Young, reviewing the festival for the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Daily_Echo" title="Bournemouth Daily Echo">
        Bournemouth Daily Echo
       </a>
      </i>
      , said "Faryl Smith was my personal highlight of the Thursday night line-up, her bizarrely powerful voice (considering her diminutive size and age) taking my breath away and it contrasted so well with her naivete as she said 'at least it's not raining'  just as the heavens opened."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In October Smith performed for the first time in Ireland, at the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Concert_Hall" title="National Concert Hall">
       National Concert Hall
      </a>
      , Dublin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She continued to perform publicly throughout 2011. In May, she performed at a
      <a href="/wiki/Help_for_Heroes" title="Help for Heroes">
       Help for Heroes
      </a>
      charity concert, which raised 2,000,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in both June and October, she performed at concerts to celebrate the 90th year of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_British_Legion" title="Royal British Legion">
       Royal British Legion
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She again appeared at the Llangollen International Musical Eisteddfod in July, where she sang with
      <a href="/wiki/Russell_Watson" title="Russell Watson">
       Russell Watson
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-with_top_tenor_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-with_top_tenor-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith's father described the appearance as "like a homecoming", due to her previous appearance at the competition.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-with_top_tenor_77-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-with_top_tenor-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In further charitable events later in the year, she raised 2,700 for a hospice in
      <a href="/wiki/Cransley" title="Cransley">
       Cransley
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and performed in aid of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" title="Salvation Army">
       Salvation Army
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">
       Portsmouth
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the Christmas period, Smith performed for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital_Children%27s_Charity" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital Children's Charity">
       Great Ormond Street Hospital Children's Charity
      </a>
      in their annual Christmas carol concert,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at the North Wales Choral Festival at
      <a href="/wiki/Llandudno" title="Llandudno">
       Llandudno
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She also appeared as a guest on
      <a href="/wiki/Rhydian_Roberts" title="Rhydian Roberts">
       Rhydian Roberts
      </a>
      's talent show on
      <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">
       S4C
      </a>
      in December.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2012, she performed with the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mousehole_Male_Voice_Choir&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mousehole Male Voice Choir (page does not exist)">
       Mousehole Male Voice Choir
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Penzance" title="Penzance">
       Penzance
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in 2013, she continued to perform locally in Kettering.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From 2012-3, Smith performed several times with the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Harp_Ensemble&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Harp Ensemble (page does not exist)">
       International Harp Ensemble
      </a>
      , a Surrey-based group of harpists who produce a variety of different styles of harp music,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harp_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harp-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including appearing with the group on a September episode of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Songs_of_Praise" title="Songs of Praise">
        Songs of Praise
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She also guest-featured on the group's 2012 album
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Magic_of_a_Thousand_Strings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Magic of a Thousand Strings (page does not exist)">
        The Magic of a Thousand Strings
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harp_85-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harp-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      singing on five tracks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_59-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edge-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Further shows with the International Harp Ensemble are planned into 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While working with the International Harp Ensemble, Smith began training with vocal coach
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joy_Mammen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joy Mammen (page does not exist)">
       Joy Mammen
      </a>
      , who also teaches
      <a href="/wiki/Lesley_Garrett" title="Lesley Garrett">
       Lesley Garrett
      </a>
      , as well as learning German and Italian, with the intention of moving from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_crossover" title="Classical crossover">
       classical crossover
      </a>
      towards
      <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">
       opera
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_59-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edge-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">
       Personal life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faryl_Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Personal life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Smith was born in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kettering,_Northamptonshire" title="Kettering, Northamptonshire">
       Kettering, Northamptonshire
      </a>
      , England, on 23 July 1995. She originally attended Henry Gotch Primary School in Kettering and then became a student at
      <a href="/wiki/Southfield_School,_Kettering" title="Southfield School, Kettering">
       Southfield School for Girls
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seven_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-seven-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      although she received private tutoring while working.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Once_upon_91-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Once_upon-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She completed her
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GCSE" title="GCSE">
       GCSEs
      </a>
      in 2011,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and she studied for her
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_levels" title="A levels">
       A levels
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Welsh_X_Factor_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Welsh_X_Factor-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the intention of going to university afterwards.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, she is going to instead try for the
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music" title="Royal Academy of Music">
       Royal Academy of Music
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-All_grown_up_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-All_grown_up-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While at school, Smith enjoyed playing football; she played for the Kettering Generals Under-11s girls' team when they reached the
      <a href="/wiki/Weetabix" title="Weetabix">
       Weetabix
      </a>
      League cup final, as well as for the club's Under-13 girls.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FA_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FA-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She attended a theatre club, played the guitar and piano and sang in two choirs,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budding_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-budding-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including the Masquerade Youth Choir.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith's father, Tony, is a health and safety inspector,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_59-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edge-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and for a time worked full-time overseeing Smith's activities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Once_upon_91-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Once_upon-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Her mother, Linda, is a hairdresser,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_59-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edge-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and she has an older brother, Shea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Once_upon_91-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Once_upon-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
